 ฐ ฐ ฐ  ฿฿฿ฐ  ฐฐฐ ฐฐ ฐ  ฐฐ     ฐ  ฐฐ ฿ฐ ฐฐฐ
     ฿       ฿       ฐ                 
              ฿          ฐ  ฿   ฿
    ฿ฐ ฿       ฿     ฿        ฿   ฐ฿ ฿ฐ     ฿฿฿฿
         ฐ฿฿฿฿฿฿  i n t r o ! ฿฿฿ฐ฿ฐ     ฿      ฿
                                          ฿

 ษออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออป
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ    Author  : The RCN Editor Staff                                          บ
 บ    Subject : Introduction                                                  บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 ศออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออผ
 ษออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออป
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ      Welcome to Reality Check Network, your #1 Warez E-mag!  And so we'd   บ
 บ  like to stay!  Currently, we have just finished wiping out the            บ
 บ  competition, apparently it just couldn't compete with us.  However, this  บ
 บ  extra burst of confidence seems to be our worst enemy thus far.  We       บ
 บ  noticed this after the release of Issue #21.  The editors, and some of    บ
 บ  the readers, noticed that the ways of RCN needed to be fixed and          บ
 บ  upgraded.  In retrospect to earlier issues, RCN was still getting         บ
 บ  bigger, but size isn't everything when it comes to an e-mag.  It was      บ
 บ  becoming obvious that we were sacrificing quality for a bigger magazine.  บ
 บ  Furthermore, the ethics of RCN also needed ramification, as inspired by   บ
 บ  Rio & Ken's letter, and those of several other people.                    บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ      In trying to keep RCN's position as the #1 warez e-mag, the editors   บ
 บ  have agreed upon several modifications that we think will please you,     บ
 บ  the readers, today and in the future.  We believe that the set of pacts   บ
 บ  we have agreed to will create a more harmonious relationship between RCN  บ
 บ  and its readers, and make reading RCN a more enjoyable embarkment.  A     บ
 บ  major difference that you will notice between this issue of RCN and       บ
 บ  previous issues is that we no longer strive for 8 articles, and 8         บ
 บ  interviews.  We all know that reading repeated interviews was getting     บ
 บ  boring, and we all know that articles about mere fluff were never         บ
 บ  interesting.  Obviously a person that doesn't read anything because he    บ
 บ  hates to do so will never enjoy RCN, but people that do enjoy reading     บ
 บ  were starting to get frustrated with the layout of the above sections.    บ
 บ  So now, we will have a fluctuating number of articles and interviews,     บ
 บ  with much greater scrutiny based on quality.  RCN's old philosophy was    บ
 บ  based on giving everybody a voice, but if a person is educated enough to  บ
 บ  form an opinion on any given topic, he should be educated enough to       บ
 บ  write a well structured article to support his case.                      บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ      You will also find a new ADDITION to RCN in this issue.  I am         บ
 บ  speaking of the "Cover Story" menu!  In previous issues, we have          บ
 บ  included the cover story within either the articles or interviews menu.   บ
 บ  Now, we will be spending a much greater amount of time on researching     บ
 บ  and studying the week's cover story.  A cover story deserves more than    บ
 บ  just an article or an interview, it deserves a complete assessment and    บ
 บ  review, something that RCN will now be able to offer.  This week's cover  บ
 บ  story is about the United Cracking Force, and you will find that the      บ
 บ  menu contains over 3 times as much information as previous issues of RCN  บ
 บ  did.                                                                      บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ      Another issue that readers were beginning to complain about in past   บ
 บ  issues is that of RCN putting people down, and constantly "dissing" on    บ
 บ  people in the scene.  It was becoming like a "soap opera," as some would  บ
 บ  phrase it.  Though I find that as somewhat humorous, I don't find it the  บ
 บ  least bit necessary, and this attitude will be done away with now and in  บ
 บ  the future.  If a person messes up and does something that's not very     บ
 บ  respectable in the scene, we will just stop reporting things that may     บ
 บ  concern that person.  The lack of publicity will be punishment enough.    บ
 บ  If a group messes up, it will only be covered if we feel that publicity   บ
 บ  and information about the group could raise its potential to survive.     บ
 บ  If a problem is more serious than that, it will not be RCN's position to  บ
 บ  correct it, but rather the scene's as a whole.                            บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ      Now for meeting logs.  We were the first to use them, and they have   บ
 บ  done a most amazing job of showing us who people REALLY are behind        บ
 บ  "closed doors."  But enough of them now.  I will use GODS as an example   บ
 บ  because it is a group that has since split up and probably won't mind a   บ
 บ  bit of publication about them.  RCN obtained the first meeting log of     บ
 บ  GODS when it was initially grouping.  This is something I would say is    บ
 บ  NOT our position to publish.  It solely contained information about the   บ
 บ  organization of the group, something that they are quite entitled to do.  บ
 บ  However, the latter meeting log about GODS would be something I think we  บ
 บ  should have the right to publish, for one important reason.  The latter   บ
 บ  log effected people beyond just GODS members.  It contained information   บ
 บ  that could hinder the rest of the scene, and that's not right.  So that   บ
 บ  was something that people did deserve to see.  From now on, no meeting    บ
 บ  logs will be published, even if they are just two people cussing each     บ
 บ  other out, if they don't contain data that could severely hinder the      บ
 บ  scene and outside members.                                                บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ      For example, and note that this is purely hypothetical, I have utter  บ
 บ  respect for the groups I am about to name.  Let's say Hybrid had a        บ
 บ  meeting about how they were really pissed off about the Dynamix           บ
 บ  incident.  That would NOT be something that RCN could publish.  Hybrid    บ
 บ  is quite entitled to talk amongst themselves.  However, if Hybrid were    บ
 บ  talking about how Razor is really pissing them off and how they're about  บ
 บ  to start a masterful plan to grab all the Razor suppliers, and let's say  บ
 บ  that Razor didn't know about this, now THAT would be something RCN        บ
 บ  should publish.  The distinction?  Hybrid would be crossing over the      บ
 บ  "Hybrid" boundary and stepping over the feet of others.                   บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ      I would like to make an important clarification and apology to        บ
 บ  several people/groups that deserved it a long time ago.  I would like to  บ
 บ  apologize to the readers of RCN that have been in disagreement with us    บ
 บ  in past times.  However, I use this as an example to you that we DO read  บ
 บ  your mail and ARE interested in what you have to say.  Rio & Ken sent us  บ
 บ  clear mail that explained his position with examples, and he was right,   บ
 บ  and we were wrong, and now we're fixing our mistakes.  You can't expect   บ
 บ  us to change, however, if you never send us any comments.                 บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ      Lastly, I would like to make an apology to Prestige and The Renegade  บ
 บ  Chemist together.  Though the news is rather old, it is news that makes   บ
 บ  a difference today, and makes a difference in the reputation of TRC, and  บ
 บ  it deserves to be said.  A while back, RCN published information          บ
 บ  regarding TRC and Dynamix, and his departure from Dynamix into Prestige.  บ
 บ  However, we never really gave TRC a chance to explain his side of the     บ
 บ  story by himself.  Since then, Prestige has placed a boycott on RCN,      บ
 บ  viewable on their WWW page, which stated that they would not be granting  บ
 บ  RCN any interviews.  Since their boycott, RCN DID get two interviews      บ
 บ  with Prestige leaders, but despite that, we still want to clear our       บ
 บ  grounds with Prestige as a whole.  So, I apologize to TRC for not giving  บ
 บ  him the opportunity to fully express himself in the matters at hand, he   บ
 บ  is a great help to the scene, he is an agressive person, but that's not   บ
 บ  a negative thing in the scene.  Furthermore, I would like to extend that  บ
 บ  apology to Prestige all together, and as a result, I have published       บ
 บ  TRC's side of the matter in the articles menu.                            บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ      Again, you can always find Reality Check Network available on the     บ
 บ  WWW at HTTP://WWW.RCN.ORG/INDEX.HTML, as well as find some of our         บ
 บ  previous competition (though, unfortunately, none exists at the moment)   บ
 บ  and perhaps compare and contrast.  And as a final note, a little word     บ
 บ  about etiquette, purposefully placed at the END of the introduction.  I   บ
 บ  don't mind if you don't want to read an entire article or interview, and  บ
 บ  decide you've had enough in the middle, but if you're going to contact    บ
 บ  us with a complaint, make sure you HAVE read the entire text before       บ
 บ  doing so.  It doesn't look too impressive when you complain about         บ
 บ  something and our response to your complaint was in the body of the text  บ
 บ  all the while, but you were too lazy to find it.                          บ

 ษออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออป
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ  Dear RCN,                                                                 บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ      Basically, everyone knows that RCN rules so I'm not going to even     บ
 บ  say it.  Alright, fine then, OK!, I will say it, RCN RULES! (Be a bitch   บ
 บ  about it why don't you.)  Anyway, this letter is to comment on the way I  บ
 บ  feel about THE scene, and to react to what people say about it.           บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ      Firstly, I want to talk about the couriers of the world.  Quite a     บ
 บ  few years ago, when 14.4 modems were top of the line, BBS traders were    บ
 บ  judged on the quality of warez that they spread, not HOW MUCH they        บ
 บ  spread.  Now, with the introduction of the Internet SCENE a great         บ
 บ  courier is someone that can move over a gig, or so, a week between a few  บ
 บ  places.  That's all honky dory, but if it's something to help you learn   บ
 บ  your A-B-C's, or something that doesn't install correctly, I honestly     บ
 บ  DOUBT that it is useful to anyone in 'the scene.'                         บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ      A great courier is someone who has tested the warez which they are    บ
 บ  spreading, know that they are quality, and starts the batch.  I know for  บ
 บ  Internet couriers this is extremely hard since they hardly ever download  บ
 บ  the program themselves, but for BBS traders it only takes a quick 10      บ
 บ  minutes to see if it works before they pass it along.  Anyone, namely 10  บ
 บ  year old little pricks, can go to bed and leave their computers on,       บ
 บ  uploading all night... THAT takes no talent, and deserves NO respect.     บ
 บ  You people might not realize this, but groups NEED their couriers.  They  บ
 บ  need quality people to spread their lovely working game or util.  Now     บ
 บ  think about it this way.                                                  บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ      Wouldn't a group LOVE to hire someone that they knew tested shit      บ
 บ  before they spread it.  This would ENSURE the group not getting           บ
 บ  embarassed if they happen to fuck up a release.  Also, if something       บ
 บ  doesn't work people complaining, saying that the groups 'SUCKS', and      บ
 บ  give them all the blame.  Well, my friends, that's BULLSHIT!  The people  บ
 บ  who spread bad shit are as much at fault as the ones who packaged it.     บ
 บ  The attitude of most traders right now is....... "Hmm... I should really  บ
 บ  see if this works before I spend 14 hours uploading it... but what the    บ
 บ  hell!  I wanna download that cool program so fuck it."  To all of you     บ
 บ  who think/do that... I hope that the program you download was uploaded    บ
 บ  by a prick like you.                                                      บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ      Secondly, although I can bullshit about the scene and its problems    บ
 บ  for hours upon hours I would just like to touch on one more major issue.  บ
 บ  In one of the previous magazines (I forgot which one) someone commented   บ
 บ  on the BBS scene deteriorating while the Internet scene thrives.  In      บ
 บ  most respects that's true.  BUT... look at it this way, a long time ago   บ
 บ  when someone wanted respect in 'the scene' they either were a GREAT       บ
 บ  coder, courier or sysop of a popular board.  So every little dumbfuck     บ
 บ  would pick the one they thought was the best.  In this case I'll use the  บ
 บ  BBS.  They would beg their parents for a phone line, put up a BBS, and    บ
 บ  hope it would thrive.  Sucking up to the right people, while getting      บ
 บ  help in the process, would sometimes make it prosper, in turn making      บ
 บ  them popular.  Now, ok, I know I'm exagerating, but it gets better.       บ
 บ  With the Internet here, groups are practically BEGGING for Internet       บ
 บ  couriers, so these little losers put down their boards and go to a life   บ
 บ  of Internet trading, usually changing their already stupid handle to      บ
 บ  something stupidier in the process.  This, in my view, can only make the  บ
 บ  BBS scene STRONGER.  Sure it'll mean there are fewer BBSes around,        บ
 บ  but...it also is a method of 'trimming the fat'.. getting rid of the      บ
 บ  people who are too weak or disloyal to stay in, and making the remaining  บ
 บ  BBSers/BBSes the 'TRUE ELiTE!'.  Phew, glad I got that off my chest.      บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ      Last, I know I'm blabbering on, but hey.. you can always hit ESC.     บ
 บ  Anyway, in another issue someone said that RCN magazine is making it      บ
 บ  unsafe for the scene.  That is just stupid and moronic.  RCN is the       บ
 บ  collection of articles of people who are on IRC and bullshit like that.   บ
 บ  This means that basically RCN is a colorful snapspot of a night on IRC.   บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ                                               Signed,                      บ
 บ                                                  The Insane Sicilian       บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 วฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤถ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ  The Insane Sicilian,                                                      บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ      Ooh, a colorful snapshot!  "And I present to you this week's kodak    บ
 บ  moment, the United Cracking Force!"  Heheheh...                           บ

 บ  Dear RCN,                                                                 บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ      You know, I was sitting at home the other night, reading RCN #19,     บ
 บ  when something hit me.  "Chris Carter?!? Getting busted?!?!  Whoa, this   บ
 บ  is real.  This is reality."  BLAM!  The reality train struck me right in  บ
 บ  between the eyez.  But, here in mah sleepy town in Kentucky, you don't    บ
 บ  hear of computer crime.  We had a bank hacked, but I seriously doubt      บ
 บ  that that was local, I assumed it was some long distance phreaker, war    บ
 บ  dailing through the 82 prefix.                                            บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ      But, then I read on.  The article said he was busted also.  Hmmm...   บ
 บ  sounds like he wasn't so leet after all.  But, the article also said he   บ
 บ  WAS in the scene pretty big when he went down.  Hmmm... sounds like he    บ
 บ  got sloppy.  I mean, we all know the risk, we assume it every time we     บ
 บ  type "mget *.*".  If you are under 18, you can mess your life up          บ
 บ  something awful, and if you are older, the same can happen.  But we all   บ
 บ  are risk takers.  We ARE the cyber pirates that all of the magazines      บ
 บ  talk about.  We are all famous or infamous, depends on how you look at    บ
 บ  it.                                                                       บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ      Back to my small town.  I was mowing, and thinking, you know, I have  บ
 บ  some underage friends, whose parents are COPS and they are in big on      บ
 บ  warez.  Hmmm... crooked cops?  Never... always.  In a small town,         บ
 บ  corruption (big enough for NYC)?  I mean, my town was once voted the      บ
 บ  easiest place to get away with a crime.  We have the HIGHEST unsolved     บ
 บ  crime rate for a town our size.  So, shall I dare say I am at LESS of a   บ
 บ  risk than the rest of my warez buds in Core?  I don't know.               บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ      Actually, I don't see any "World's Laws", which would have to be      บ
 บ  made to police CyberSpace since you check the U.S. laws at the door, or   บ
 บ  your respective countries, that say I can't do this or that.  I mean, I   บ
 บ  may move stuff from Sweden to Japan, all from an account in Australia.    บ
 บ  I was never in the U.S. this whole time, but I am tried if caught by US   บ
 บ  computer laws.  Is this fair?  Well, to them "Big Blue" it is.            บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ      Anything that steals $45 dollars from someone that put a bunch of     บ
 บ  1's and 0's in a pattern that made this alien splatter blood all over my  บ
 บ  screen when I shot him with a M 16.  I mean, there is a chance <1 in 1    บ
 บ  000 000 000> that I could randomly write binary that would replicate      บ
 บ  this last scene from a well known 3D game.  I mean, who is the thief      บ
 บ  here?  Us or them?  They charge $50 for a piece of plastic and some       บ
 บ  magnetic tape, and I AM THE CRIMINAL for getting it for free?             บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ      Well, I won't run on too long, I just can't see where some of these   บ
 บ  old fogey Congressmen get off saying what is right and wrong in           บ
 บ  CyberSpace, when they can't point and click through a Wet Winbloez 95.    บ
 บ  Well, I hope I get to write this every week or so, about my area warez    บ
 บ  scene, or lack of, and my general opinion (I have one for everything) on  บ
 บ  stuff in CyberSpace.                                                      บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ                                               Signed,                      บ
 บ                                                  Da Phreak                 บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 วฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤถ
 บ                                                                            บ

 บ  on IRC.  I'm sure you will tell me that you're not an ALL bad IRC op and  บ

 ษออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออป
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ  Dear RCN,                                                                 บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ      As an avid Internet courier myself, I know how succesful it can be.   บ
 บ  However, others disagree.  IRC couriering is mostly couriering through    บ
 บ  DCC.  People set up offer bots, place them in channels like #Exceed,      บ
 บ  #M8leech and #Phatfiles, have them display lists of stuff their           บ
 บ  offering, and people leech stuff.  This is one of the most efficient      บ
 บ  ways of couriering and is also the easiest to measure success in.         บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ      In BBS and FTP couriering, you can usually only see how much someone  บ
 บ  uploaded, you can't always see which files are the most popular, or how   บ
 บ  many people leeched them.  With IRC couriering, your bot can tell you     บ
 บ  exactly how many megs have been leeched and how many times people have    บ
 บ  downloaded each file.  This allows IRC couriers to see what files are     บ
 บ  the most popular and which to offer again.  With FTP and BBS couriering,  บ
 บ  you could upload a gig of shit and you'd still get credit for uploading   บ
 บ  it, even if no one downloaded it.  Another plus is the publicity the      บ
 บ  group gets.  It's fairly simple to add a file at the end of an offer      บ
 บ  list containing an app or an nfo, and groups gain lots of notariety that  บ
 บ  way.                                                                      บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ      The downsides to it are the complexity of getting things together.    บ
 บ  First, you have to find a shell with IRC, upload the stuff you want to    บ
 บ  offer, then get an XDCC offer script (fphoenix.irc is known as the best   บ
 บ  all-around and is the most popular), and then configure the offer list.   บ
 บ  Also, people who run them will sometimes get messages from people who     บ
 บ  are having problems.  I once had someone who said, "I can't download      บ
 บ  this file because it keeps stopping and saying I'm not fast enough, but   บ
 บ  I have a 14.4 modem!"  I politely explained the system of minimum speeds  บ
 บ  (which I never set porpously more than 1K/s, unlike the fATE couriers     บ
 บ  who have 3K/s as the minimum, jack asses), and said that he'd probably    บ
 บ  need atleast a 28.8 modem.                                                บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ      He continued to bug me, and finally I sent him the file manually,     บ
 บ  just to get him to shut up.  This is REALLY annoying after a while, but   บ
 บ  we IRC couriers have to put up with it.  In addition, groups with IRC     บ
 บ  channels will often get dumbasses in their rooms saying, "How come this   บ
 บ  thing doesn't work on my 386?"  OK, maybe that's a little extreme, but    บ
 บ  you get the picture.                                                      บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ      Personally I feel that the good outweighs the bad and that IRC        บ
 บ  couriering has a bright future.  Just take a look at all the offer        บ
 บ  channels springing up and becoming popular.  #Phatfiles was only          บ
 บ  recently founded, and it's already very popular and many IRC couriering   บ
 บ  groups support it.  I feel that it would be extremely peneficial to       บ
 บ  couriering groups such as Everlast and RiSC to add IRC divisions to       บ
 บ  their groups.  But if that doesn't happen, groups like PTA will continue  บ
 บ  to dominate the IRC couriering arena.                                     บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ                                               Signed,                      บ
 บ                                                  Ermac                     บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 ศออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออผ

 บ                                                                            บ
 บ  Dear RCN,                                                                 บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ      A dupe.  The most hated thing in a release group with the only        บ
 บ  exception possibly being a non-working release.  In the past, dupes have  บ
 บ  been taken care of in medieval style fashion by getting axed.  After a    บ
 บ  succession of dupes, a group's entire label might get nuked {ie.          บ
 บ  BLD*.zip for a group with the acronym BLD}.  This possibly group          บ
 บ  threatening reputation is not looked upon well by groups, and is feared   บ
 บ  to the point of insanity.  So, my question is, what should be done about  บ
 บ  dupes?  Let's take a look at my plan if you will.                         บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ      Many dupes are done due to the limit of BBS couriering.  For          บ
 บ  instance, a local group releases a game (way over the 50 disk limit) in   บ
 บ  Australia.  This release does not travel well outside Australia, only     บ
 บ  gets to Russia, and stops there.  Another group, later that month,        บ
 บ  releases the same game after dupe checking extensively throughout its     บ
 บ  sites, RCN listings, and BBSes, and finds that the game was not           บ
 บ  released.  After a few days, this release (under the 50 disk limit) is    บ
 บ  spread all the way across the world and eventually reaches the point of   บ
 บ  where the local group released it.  During this process of the release    บ
 บ  crossing over to the other territory, the dupe is noticed, and            บ
 บ  eventually word gets around that the group that released it under the     บ
 บ  limit duped the release.  This scenario has happened many a time, and is  บ
 บ  just not possible to outwit 100% of the time.  In my opinion, a group     บ
 บ  should not be denounced for a dupe that was not effectively spread by     บ
 บ  the original group.  Also, a group should not be denounced for duping a   บ
 บ  release that was not released under the 50 disk limit.  If I'm a          บ
 บ  supplier for a worldwide group, and I am based in the United States, how  บ
 บ  am I supposed to find out about some release that was released in         บ
 บ  Australia by a no-name group?                                             บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ      Here is my proposition, any game that goes over the 50 disk limit     บ
 บ  (actual game) should not be counted as an actual release.  Also, if a     บ
 บ  group releases addons to that game, and they go over 100 disks, then the  บ
 บ  addons should not be counted.  If a release group re-releases these       บ
 บ  games/addons under the limit, then they are in no violation of the        บ
 บ  rules.  In order to limit the number of dupes on viable games, all games  บ
 บ  must hit a certain Internet Site, and BBS that is widely known in the     บ
 บ  scene to everyone.  If it is not uploaded there by the time the other     บ
 บ  group releases the game, then it is not considered a viable release, and  บ
 บ  the other group may release it.                                           บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ                                               Signed,                      บ
 บ                                                  Genocide                  บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ                                                                            บ

 บ      A famous quote I can think of, "Can't we all just get along?"  After  บ
 บ  joining a few channels, and being involved in the underground scene for   บ
 บ  10 years, I have seen some good groups come and go.                       บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ      You see the BBS scene vs. the Internet scene is totally different,    บ
 บ  in the BBS scene, you don't see people blasting the groups that courier   บ
 บ  to the boards there.  If fact, most people praise the courier's work in   บ
 บ  uploading a few hundred megs of files to a board.  No one ever said fuck  บ
 บ  this group, this group sucks because they bite off of this group.         บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ      However, in the Internet scene thats all I see now in most of these   บ
 บ  channels.  If its ragging on ROR for duplication of Quake Beta 3 Full     บ
 บ  Release, and stripping the beta logo out, or if its for Hybrid releasing  บ
 บ  a game with a few fixes that have to come later (Warcraft 2).  Better     บ

 บ  Dear RCN,                                                                 บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ      This article or opinion column is something that me and a few others  บ
 บ  have started to notice.  I am the IRC Coordinator of Asylum 96 which is   บ
 บ  a releasing group which is officially couriered by NvC.  I am also a      บ
 บ  courier of AOD.  I have seen two very different styles of couriering.     บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ      NvC, New Vision Couiers, has about 3 private sites that they get      บ
 บ  their warez to.  Then what they do is get dumps.  For all of you who      บ
 บ  don't know what a dump is, it is a anonymous site where people upload     บ
 บ  lots of warez.  When the site is full, it is released to the public so    บ
 บ  that they may all have access to it and download a much as they want.     บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ      AOD, Angels of Death, on the other hand has about 7or 8 private       บ
 บ  sites.  Many of these sites even have ratios on them.  But it is a very   บ
 บ  closed circle.  The warez come into the circle but they don't come out.   บ
 บ  People courier to the sites just in the circle and nothing is going out   บ
 บ  to those bottom of the ground leechers.                                   บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ      Now when u look in #Exceed or #M8leech or #Phatfiles, you see         บ
 บ  offerers.  Well these offerers are the main way of getting warez out to   บ
 บ  the general public.  I see offer bots there 24 hours a day, 7 days a      บ
 บ  week, so people can get the latest is 0 day.  I know that NvC has lots    บ
 บ  of offer bots run by one man, |ACiD|, who has about 5 gigs leeched every  บ
 บ  day.  Nobody knows him but a few.  AOD does not support their offerers    บ
 บ  very much.  Groups have really scaled back on the offerers.  Groups have  บ
 บ  about 1 or 2 dedicated offerers and that is it.  The whole public gets    บ
 บ  to know the group through releases, sites, or offerers.                   บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ      The average Joe never see the big 2 gig t3, 0 hour private site, but  บ
 บ  does this mean he can't have access to the latest in warez?  I dont       บ
 บ  think so.  0 day warez are usually found from offerers.  They aren't      บ
 บ  usually found on anonymous sites or site lists.  You can find the warez   บ
 บ  after about 1 week on a list or a site.  Unless it is something big like  บ
 บ  Duke Nukem 3D.                                                            บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ      To the average Joe, IRC offerers are some of the best things.  They   บ
 บ  give out warez for FREE!  They don't expect a site in return, a shell,    บ
 บ  another game or util, or even a thank you.  AOD has not supported their   บ
 บ  offerers well at all.  We don't have a dedicated 0 hour non-ratio site    บ
 บ  for us to download and offer from.  I have to wait until someone finally  บ
 บ  uploads it to a non-ratio site to download it and offer it.  I know I     บ
 บ  try to do my share of uploading but I never get there in time to upload   บ
 บ  stuff before the super courier does.                                      บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ      In conclusion, I would like to say that groups should do whatever it  บ
 บ  takes to have fun.  Second, I would like to groups to be more public and  บ
 บ  open, this can be do with offerers or dump sites.  People will know you   บ
 บ  if you give them what they want.  Take their requests into                บ
 บ  consideration.  I would also like to say that the scene is very           บ
 บ  cluttered right now.  Not with the nice people but the ones who want an   บ
 บ  edge over the other guy by spying or something.  Remember we can all get  บ
 บ  along if we try!                                                          บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ                                               Signed,                      บ
 บ                                                  Rip-Kord                  บ
 บ                                                                            บ

 บ  Dear RCN,                                                                 บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ      For more information on a quota shell, all the user needs to do to    บ
 บ  find out where he/she can store da huge files is simply type              บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ      "quota"                                                               บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ      This will tell him/her where he/she is limited to hd space.  Most     บ
 บ  providers do not allocate all thier drives to quotas.  Ie they mess up    บ
 บ  and not quota thier WWW drives and so on.  If they want to get a          บ
 บ  complete list of all the drives thier provider offers then they simply    บ
 บ  type                                                                      บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ      "df"                                                                  บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ      This will list ALL drives that are mounted on the system.  Just       บ
 บ  compare it with the quota listing and see what they have quotas on and    บ
 บ  what drives they don't.                                                   บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ      And if ALL drives are quotaed, they simply go to the /tmp or /temp    บ
 บ  directories.  Hitex was wrong in just saying /temp, because some          บ
 บ  providers using BSD dont have /temp they have /tmp.                       บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ      Also a little hint, if you store files in the /temp /tmp directory    บ
 บ  don't create a directory inside that and call it                          บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ      ".whatever"                                                           บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ      Make it sound offical like                                            บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ      ".systemlinks"                                                        บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ      Adding the . in front of it stops a simple ls from seeing it, and     บ
 บ  most users don't bother doing a "ls -al" to see all the files, and if it  บ
 บ  looks offical they won't bother going in there.                           บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ                                               Signed,                      บ
 บ                                                  Anonymous                 บ
 บ                                                                            บ

 บ      Violence was originally the crackers, suppliers, and couriers of      บ
 บ  NGT.  We started the release division because JLennon closed down         บ
 บ  Extreme and merged into us.  He had a lot of things he could supply so    บ
 บ  we decided on a release team.  For about 2 weeks we racked up about 15    บ
 บ  releases, which was pretty good.  It still wasn't doing as I wanted it    บ
 บ  to.  So we decided to break it off into its own release group.  The name  บ
 บ  we decided on was Violence, which Manowar had always wanted to use.       บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ      Violence did a lot better than NGT did with releasing.  We put out    บ
 บ  about 15 more releases in a couple weeks.  Still we weren't getting       บ
 บ  enough support.  Mortality duped us, and used the reason we didn't        บ
 บ  spread our releases enough.  At first I tried recruiting better           บ
 บ  couriers, etc.  The job was still not getting done.                       บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ      During the last week of Violence, several groups offered to merge us  บ
 บ  into them.  Among those were Legion and DOD.  DOD is a very experienced   บ
 บ  group but they aren't a releasing mecca as they used to be.  Legion has   บ
 บ  been doing very well in the past 2 weeks.  They have very good couriers,  บ
 บ  good sites, etc.  So we decided to merge into Legion.  We dropped a       บ
 บ  couple couriers in Violence, and brought everyone else into Legion.       บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ      From Violence, the staff positions were designated as follows.        บ
 บ  Manowar took the Council spot in Legion.  Dawg and I took senior          บ
 บ  positions, while everyone else pretty much stayed the same place as they  บ
 บ  were.                                                                     บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ      Legion is doing exceptionally well this week.  With 10 releases in    บ
 บ  the past 3 days, everyone and their mom wants to join.  We are not        บ
 บ  accepting any couriers at the moment.  We are going to be the best util   บ
 บ  group in the scene.  'Nuff said.                                          บ

 ษออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออป
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ    Author  : Hitex                                                         บ
 บ    Subject : UCF Fixing Others' Mistakes                                   บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 ศออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออผ
 ษออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออป
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ      Recently Mortality, a very respected utils releasing force, released  บ
 บ  "Omnipage Pro v7.0 for Windows 95."  Omnipage pro is an OCR (Optical      บ
 บ  Character Recognition, or something like that) program useful if you      บ
 บ  have a scanner.  It will help you scan, and, if scanning text pages,      บ
 บ  will convert the text into letters known by the computer as a font.       บ
 บ  This will make the document editable in a word processor.  This is an     บ
 บ  awesome program, and I quickly jumped on the release to download it.  I   บ
 บ  finished downloading it, ran setup, everything was looking good, until    บ
 บ  it got to the serial number.  In Windows 95, I started another DOS        บ
 บ  prompt and opened up the MTY.NFO file.  I looked for the serial number,   บ
 บ  entered it, and proud that it worked, continued on.  Then I couldn't get  บ
 บ  it to recognize that I had disk1 in a "disk1" directory.  Dumb program.   บ
 บ  I went back to the NFO file just to find that I had to put the thing on   บ
 บ  floppies to install it.  Who ever has 5 floppies lying around any more?   บ
 บ  5 ZIP disks maybe, but the last time I saw a floppy disk, I was a little  บ
 บ  boy!  I was pissed off, so I cancelled everything and went online trying  บ
 บ  to find some Mortality senior I could vent my anger out on.  Mortality    บ
 บ  didn't even bother to crack their release.                                บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ      Unable to do so (maybe they were hiding!) I found a guy from UCF who  บ
 บ  told me that UCF had just released a crack to fix the release.  My        บ
 บ  thoughts quickly shifted from cussing out Mortality to getting the        บ
 บ  program to work!  I downloaded the crack, and surely enough, everything   บ
 บ  worked.  In fact, I don't remember ever having downloaded a crack by UCF  บ
 บ  and having it not work.  No UCF member ever came up to Mortality and      บ
 บ  yelled at them, no UCF member shouted at them for not doing something so  บ
 บ  simple as finding a cracker (UCF would have done it if asked), UCF        บ
 บ  quietly took the release and, without any fuss, released a crack just a   บ
 บ  little while later.                                                       บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ      UCF has always been one to chase after releases and fix others'       บ
 บ  fuckups, it has been done almost religiously, and never have I seen a     บ
 บ  member of UCF yell at any group for messing up.  UCF takes requests with  บ
 บ  open arms, but that's like offering a drug addict free rehabilitation.    บ
 บ  Mortality's reason for releasing a half-working release wasn't because    บ
 บ  they couldn't find a cracker, it was because they wanted to be fast       บ
 บ  about it.                                                                 บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ      UCF has done a wonderful job of cracking programs for the scene for   บ
 บ  2 years now.  They've seen many groups come and go, yet they have hung    บ
 บ  on, and quite well I might add.  A few groups are blessed with having a   บ
 บ  few crackers from UCF as their own members, DOD quite blessed with        บ
 บ  having Misha as a member, and it's true, I haven't seen any uncracked     บ
 บ  DOD releases as long as I remember.                                       บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ      So let's all congratulate one of the scene's truly finest groups,     บ
 บ  and give the United Cracking Force a big round of applause, a much        บ
 บ  deserved one after two years of consistent cracking, and there's no end   บ
 บ  in sight.  Thank you for all the work you have done for us, UCF, and      บ
 บ  keep it up, you're doing a wonderful job!                                 บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 ศออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออผ

         ฿       ฿    ฿       ฿ ฿
    ฿  ฐ฿    ฿฿฿฿฿      ฿ ฐ    ฿฿฿฿฿   ฿฿    ฿ฐ฿
  ฿฿฿ฐ฿฿     ฿     ฿                       ฿฿฿
        ฿              i  n  t  e  r  v  i  e  w  s !

 ษออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออป
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ    Reporter : Rebel Chicken             Interviewee : Marquis              บ
 บ    Subject  : UCF President             Affiliation : UCF!                 บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 ศออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออผ
 ษออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออป
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ RCN: UCF (United Cracking Force) has been an integral part of the scene  บ
 บ        for many years now, yet it is one of the most unappreciated groups  บ
 บ        for a group that does so much.  UCF handles much of the cracking    บ
 บ        that goes on for the scene.  Could you tell us how UCF came about   บ
 บ        and why this group is important for the survival of the scene?      บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ UCF: UCF was founded in the beginning of 1994 by just 2 crackers, Sonic  บ
 บ        and me.  We were the former crackers in the well known group UTG    บ
 บ        (United Traders of Germany).  One day in 1994, UTG began to die     บ
 บ        slowly, that was the time I talked with Sonic, a hell of a cracker  บ
 บ        even today, about building our own group.  I always wanted to have  บ
 บ        my own group, and that was how it started.  We only release cracks  บ
 บ        and nothing else.                                                   บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ RCN: Does UCF release cracks solely for shareware games and utils?       บ
 บ        I've seen a few DOD (Drink or Die) and PWA (Pirates with            บ
 บ        Attitudes) utils cracked by UCF, does UCF do special crack          บ
 บ        requests for these big utils groups?                                บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ UCF: UCF released and releases cracks for any kind of software, we like  บ
 บ        or we get requests.  Mostly we crack what is uncracked but could    บ
 บ        be needed by a lot of people like D-Studio v4.1 or MIRC v4.52, but  บ
 บ        sometimes we even do cracks for well known groups to help them      บ
 บ        out.  On the other hand, most members from UCF are also in other    บ
 บ        groups such as DOD, Napalm, PWA, Prestige, and X-Force, therefore   บ
 บ        you see the names of our crackers everywhere.  If you mention       บ
 บ        DjPaul, Lost Soul, Misha, or The Riddler, they all are in other     บ
 บ        groups too.                                                         บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ RCN: I know that managing a weekly electronic magazine such as RCN is    บ
 บ        very hard and that is why RCN is one of a kind, much the same way   บ
 บ        that there is only one dominant cracking group, UCF.  I assume      บ
 บ        then that running a cracking group such as UCF must be very         บ
 บ        difficult, since there is only one cracking group that anyone has   บ
 บ        ever heard of, UCF.                                                 บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ UCF: Running UCF wasn't that hard in the beginning.  For 1 year, UCF     บ
 บ        consisted of only 2 members and even with only 5 crackers on        บ
 บ        board, it was easy.  But right now, UCF has nearly 20 members,      บ
 บ        including couriers and traders.  To tell the truth, it is a lot of  บ
 บ        work right now especially for me, because I have to coordinate a    บ
 บ        lot of things besides my own cracks, that take up a lot of my       บ
 บ        time.  I cannot recommend to do it like I do it now.                บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ RCN: I always see a lot of new courier and release groups popping up,    บ
 บ        but I rarely see new cracking groups pop up.  Why is that so?       บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ UCF: I too see a lot of new groups popping up, not even in cracking but  บ
 บ        in games and utils too.  But most of these groups come and go.      บ
 บ        UCF WILL STAY as long as I have energy, and I have a lot because I  บ
 บ        like this cracking.  And I am sure, most of us like the challenge   บ
 บ        that cracking gives us.                                             บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ RCN: How did you learn how to crack software?  Did you just pick up a    บ
 บ        book that taught you how to crack?  If so, what's the name of that  บ
 บ        book?  I want to check out that book from my local public library,  บ
 บ        but then again, I do have this really big fine and I haven't        บ
 บ        really picked up a book in a long long time.  Anyway, if it did     บ
 บ        take you something more than one book to learn how to crack, then   บ
 บ        could you describe your process in becoming a proficient cracker?   บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ UCF: In the beginning, I only read one assembler book, to get the        บ
 บ        opcodes of a program to crack.  But after 2 years, I bought the     บ
 บ        second one, MS The Programmer's PC Sourcebook!  This one was and    บ
 บ        is the most used book by me.  Nothing than plain information is in  บ
 บ        it, no damn time wasting converstation.  Other recommended books    บ
 บ        should be Win 95 and Visual C++ Stuff from Andrew Schulman and      บ
 บ        Matt Pietrek, I would not read anything else.  Beside these books,  บ
 บ        you need NU-Mega Software such as WinIce and Soft-Ice.  But in the  บ
 บ        end, your brain decides if you will become a good cracker or not.   บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ RCN: Software companies have always put cheap cd-rom and instruction     บ
 บ        manual checks on their software as a prevention to piracy.  How     บ
 บ        effective are the current protection methods?  Obviously, their     บ
 บ        software protection has yet to be very good if UCF can just take    บ
 บ        software inside out and make it usable by the average Joe.  Is      บ
 บ        there any type of software protection put out by software           บ
 บ        companies that UCF is unable to crack, a new protection of some     บ
 บ        sort that could be used to prevent piracy?                          บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ UCF: That depends on the software protection, half of the protections    บ
 บ        can be cracked in less than 30 minutes.  A third of the             บ
 บ        protections include cd-rom checks.  Both games and utils are hard   บ
 บ        to crack in the beginning, but it's nice and easy in the second     บ
 บ        try.  And that is the biggest problem, companies know a good        บ
 บ        protection is useless if it is only takes one time to crack it!     บ
 บ        But still, a tenth of all protections takes a lot of time to crack  บ
 บ        and maybe a tenth is deemed uncrackable.  To name some releases,    บ
 บ        3D-Studio for DOS, Auto CAD German, and Trade Station for Windows   บ
 บ        always took a lot of work to crack because they had very good       บ
 บ        protections.  Some programs such as DIA/DAGO are still uncracked    บ
 บ        even today.                                                         บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ RCN: There are a lot of release groups out there that release software   บ
 บ        without cracking it.  Does UCF go out of its way to help correct    บ
 บ        these misfit releases and release groups?                           บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ UCF: Sure we do, every time we install a program that we need in some    บ
 บ        way, and recognize it is uncracked, we try to crack it and release  บ
 บ        the crack a few days after the original program was released.  We   บ
 บ        do this a lot of times.  Recently, Bounds-Checker v3.0 for Win 95   บ
 บ        was released by X-Force and cracked a few days later by UCF.  We    บ
 บ        keep our eyes open and personally, I think we help the whole scene  บ
 บ        if we fix other groups' misfits.  Hopefully, I only remember a few  บ
 บ        uncracked AND important programs.                                   บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ RCN: As the President of UCF, what is your opinion of the scene?         บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ UCF: The pirate scene is really the best we could ever had.  Why?  We    บ
 บ        all help the hardware and software industry just because we exist.  บ
 บ        Without the scene, not even I would have bought a computer,         บ
 บ        because I would have to buy all the expensive software with it.     บ
 บ        Are we all rich?  No.  Software companies would sell nothing if     บ
 บ        nobody had a computer.  Even a lot of people that use a pirated     บ
 บ        programs at the age of 17 consider to buy the same software at the  บ
 บ        age of 22 for business whether they can get it cracked or not, we   บ
 บ        need them all.  I had and have a lot of nice time in the scene,     บ
 บ        and especially because I gathered a lot of real good friends in     บ
 บ        UCF.  I will not miss a single person and I will never miss the     บ
 บ        scene.                                                              บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 ศออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออผ

         ฿฿฿฿฿฿  ฿  ฿฿฿฿฿฿      ฿
         ฿       ฿    ฿       ฿ ฿
    ฿  ฐ฿    ฿฿฿฿฿      ฿ ฐ    ฿฿฿฿฿   ฿฿    ฿ฐ฿
  ฿฿฿ฐ฿฿     ฿     ฿                       ฿฿฿
        ฿              i  n  t  e  r  v  i  e  w  s !

 ษออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออป
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ    Reporter : Rebel Chicken             Interviewee : Misha                บ
 บ    Subject  : The Elvis of Cracking     Affiliation : UCF Cracker          บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 ศออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออผ
 ษออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออป
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ RCN: Many people consider you one of the best crackers in the scene.     บ
 บ        You've cracked games that were deemed uncrackable by other          บ
 บ        crackers.  Do you feel that your reputation is warranted?           บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ MSH: It probably is if the majority thinks that way.  To make it a       บ
 บ        little more clear, I'd have to consider both groups that judge me   บ
 บ        a little differently.  The two groups are crackers and general      บ
 บ        population which is consisted of non-crackers, people who don't     บ
 บ        really know what goes on behind the actual cracking process or at   บ
 บ        what level it's done.  The general public sees the results, and so  บ
 บ        far, my cracks have worked well for many people.  Also, I used to   บ
 บ        write trainers for games, which also probably raised my reputation  บ
 บ        a little for their sometimes non-standard features, I made these    บ
 บ        characters fly for example, which were not part of the original     บ
 บ        game.                                                               บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ RCN: Do you believe that you are also respected among other crackers?    บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ MSH: I believe I'm also respected among crackers, this is what matters   บ
 บ        most because only crackers can appreciate the actual work, and      บ
 บ        have a certain reputation in that community.                        บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ RCN: In your days as a cracker, even though you have had much success,   บ
 บ        which games or utils have you not been able to crack?  Of those     บ
 บ        games and utils that you have not been able to crack, what kind of  บ
 บ        protection was implemented?  If you are not able to crack such      บ
 บ        protection, do companies start using such protection more often?    บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ MSH: First of all, my cracking skills didn't stay the same all the       บ
 บ        time.  There's always room for learning and experience is a very    บ
 บ        important part of becoming better.  Hardware dongles would be       บ
 บ        considered one of the hard categories because the dongle device     บ
 บ        may contain information needed to run the program and most of the   บ
 บ        time, the cracker doesn't have access to the device itself.         บ
 บ        Script-based programs are usually considered hard to work with,     บ
 บ        things like Visual Basic for example.  Also there are several       บ
 บ        programs that attempt to stop people from tracing and cracking      บ
 บ        them by jamming debuggers, tools used to do most of the cracking,   บ
 บ        but those are very hard to write and maintain.  I still have a few  บ
 บ        programs on my list which I wasn't able to crack because of lack    บ
 บ        of experience and knowledge, most from the beginning of my          บ
 บ        cracking career, all I needed for those is some time.  And things   บ
 บ        like dongles are normally impossible to fully fix without the       บ
 บ        dongle.  I try to stay away from those types of programs.           บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ RCN: Which groups are you affiliated with besides UCF?                   บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ MSH: At this time, it's mainly UCF and probably DOD only, but I take     บ
 บ        requests from basically any group big or small so you may see me    บ
 บ        as a cracker in some nfos although I'm not officially in any other  บ
 บ        groups besides those 2.                                             บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ RCN: What's the difference between a good cracker and a good coder?      บ
 บ        Are good crackers also good coders?  And are good crackers also     บ
 บ        good coders?                                                        บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ MSH: It's interesting and although I don't immediately see the           บ
 บ        connection, but in my experience good crackers can code well at     บ
 บ        least in assembly, and frequently in other langagues.  It's         บ
 บ        different for coders I guess.  Since some assembly knowledge is     บ
 บ        required to crack, high-level-only coders can't crack and even      บ
 บ        demo-coders who code in assembly a lot may not have the             บ
 บ        experience.                                                         บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ RCN: Your cracking skills are well known, but are you also skillful in   บ
 บ        coding?  We can't all be good at everything, so don't feel          บ
 บ        embarrassed if you're not good at coding.                           บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ MSH: Actually, I'm pretty decent at coding.  I have coded some           บ
 บ        cracking-related programs such as keymakers, EXE file               บ
 บ        decompressors, tools, other programs for DOS and Windows, mostly    บ
 บ        low-level C stuff, and even attempted to write simple intros/demos  บ
 บ        in the past.                                                        บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 ศออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออผ

 บ    Reporter : Rebel Chicken             Interviewee : Manic                บ
 บ    Subject  : In Defense of Tklp        Affiliation : Reflux Senior        บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 ศออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออผ
 ษออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออออป
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ RCN: Many people in the scene now believe that ROR (Release on Rampage)  บ
 บ        and Reflux are basically the same groups with a different name,     บ
 บ        and thus, a bad ROR name might carry over to Reflux.  Do you        บ
 บ        believe that is true?  If not, why not?                             บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ RLX: Well, ROR and Reflux ARE very much alike, but when we started       บ
 บ        Reflux we brought in many new people, including a few suppliers     บ
 บ        and seniors.  We were also given a chance to start over by          บ
 บ        dropping the ROR name.  So in most cases the ban on ROR releases    บ
 บ        shouldn't carry over to becoming a ban on Reflux releases.  People  บ
 บ        who didn't like ROR probably felt that way because of members of    บ
 บ        the group, and will continue to feel that.  I know Tklp and myself  บ
 บ        have made a few enemies, so that affected some of the feelings      บ
 บ        toward ROR.                                                         บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ RCN: ROR files were banned on major boards because Tklp faked the now    บ
 บ        infamous Quake Final.  Tklp said that it was the final version of   บ
 บ        Quake even though Jay Wilbur, and other employees of iD Software    บ
 บ        would vouch for the fact that it was only the beta version hex      บ
 บ        edited to say that it was the final version.  Piston, a former      บ
 บ        senior of ROR also believes that Tklp released a fake Quake Final   บ
 บ        in an attempt to make ROR look good.  Little did Tklp realize that  บ
 บ        his choice in releasing a fake Quake Final would lead to so much    บ
 บ        hatred toward ROR.  Tklp is the leader of ROR, and he is now the    บ
 บ        leader of  Reflux.  In the eyes of the many, Reflux is still the    บ
 บ        same group led by Tklp.  What has Tklp done to warrant a second     บ
 บ        chance?                                                             บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ RLX: Tklp is a great a leader, I have stood behind him since the day     บ
 บ        ROR started and everyone criticized him for being young, saying he  บ
 บ        was to young an immature to run a stable group.  In my opinion, he  บ
 บ        isn't on a second chance, everyone makes mistakes, the release of   บ
 บ        the fake Quake Final was one of his.                                บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ RCN: Why won't he do it again?  He chose to do it once, he'll do it      บ
 บ        again.  If he does deserve a second chance, then he better put out  บ
 บ        an official apology for faking the Quake Final.  If he doesn't,     บ
 บ        not very many people will take the new ROR, Reflux, as a serious    บ
 บ        group.  If Tklp could go out of his way to fake the Quake release,  บ
 บ        what will stop him from doing it again on another game?             บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ RLX: I think that he learned his lesson the first time.  He knows the    บ
 บ        effect it had, and I doubt he would make the mistake again.         บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ RCN: Yes, he learned his lesson because he was caught.  He'll be back    บ
 บ        again.  He's been raided by the U.S. Marshalls and he still runs a  บ
 บ        pirate group, the guy's a fucking energizer bunny pirate.  I don't  บ
 บ        think he can really learn his lesson.  Moving on, I saw that        บ
 บ        Reflux had its first release a few days ago, was this release done  บ
 บ        by one of Reflux's new suppliers that were not a part of the        บ
 บ        original ROR?                                                       บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ RLX: Yes, Private Eye was supplied by Junior Mafia, a new supplier to    บ
 บ        Reflux.  Premiere, another release group, released a totally        บ
 บ        unworking copy of Private Eye.  We decided to take the oppurtunity  บ
 บ        to release a working copy and the sound addon.  We have always had  บ
 บ        strong releasing power, and will continue to.  With the new         บ
 บ        additions, Reflux will be a powerful force in the scene.            บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ RCN: I'm sure that Reflux will have a good future as a release group,    บ
 บ        after all, ROR did have some amazing releases, and I'm sure that    บ
 บ        Reflux will be able to amaze the scene in much the same way.  Have  บ
 บ        there been any problems that have come about as result of ROR       บ
 บ        changing its name to Reflux?  I do see that a few ROR seniors were  บ
 บ        dropped during the transition.  Did any of them pose a problem for  บ
 บ        Reflux?  And why were these ROR seniors cut from Reflux?  Were      บ
 บ        they part of the problem why ROR could not keep up a good           บ
 บ        reputation?                                                         บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ RLX: Well, there were no ROR seniors cut from Reflux.  Piston was a      บ
 บ        former ROR senior that left us a while back.  Piston doesn't        บ
 บ        understand the meaning of loyalty.  The other ROR senior, god,      บ
 บ        left the scene to devote more time to his business.  The rest of    บ
 บ        the ROR seniors are current Reflux seniors, with the addition of    บ
 บ        Angel of Death and Lucid.                                           บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ RCN: I'm sure that the scene will give Reflux a second chance, let's     บ
 บ        just hope that Tklp doesn't fuck up again this time.  But I do      บ
 บ        sincerely believe that Tklp needs to get off his ass and write the  บ
 บ        scene an apology letter admitting that he pulled a lame ass trick   บ
 บ        and got caught for it.  I need to hear him confess that he did      บ
 บ        wrong, and I need to hear him say that he will never pull shit      บ
 บ        like that again before I would consider him a changed man.          บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 วฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤฤถ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ      Being the editors of an e-mag, Rebel Chicken and I are forced to      บ
 บ  keep unbiased opinions about things that happen in the scene.  We can't   บ
 บ  label a group as bad because if they do change their ways, we have a      บ
 บ  duty to the scene to be there and support them once more.  As much as I   บ
 บ  tried, though, I could never keep ROR clean in my eyes.  There were too   บ
 บ  many things gone bad about them.  However, Reflux made a good move with   บ
 บ  their first release, it being a WORKING VERSION of another group's        บ
 บ  error.  I hope that this will be the future of Reflux, and I am now       บ
 บ  willing to, as my duty holds, clean ROR's marred reputation from my       บ
 บ  book, and give them another chance as Reflux.                             บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ      However, Reflux's second release, Bermuda Syndrome, turned out to be  บ
 บ  a dupe from November of 1995.  Nonetheless, Reflux showed that they were  บ
 บ  mature about it, and promptly apologized for their mistake.               บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ      Many have been bashing Reflux for, in reality, being ROR.  However,   บ
 บ  there's more in the name Reflux than meets the eye.  Reflux symbolizes    บ
 บ  not only ROR, but a second chance, something that the scene has always    บ
 บ  been an unconditional giver of.  So Tklp, and your peers, may you have a  บ
 บ  great future, and may you have learned your lesson from your previous     บ
 บ  faults, many as they may be.                                              บ
 บ                                                                            บ
 บ                                               Signed,                      บ
 บ                                                  Hitex/Rebel Chicken       บ
 บ                                                                            บ
